  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ba93e210-be2c-4a41-8545-52b3a76d279f'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4784994092180523865">1883. Thaniel Steepleton returns home to his tiny London apartment to find a gold pocket watch on his pillow. Six months later, the mysterious timepiece saves his life, drawing him away from a blast that destroys Scotland Yard. At last, he goes in search of its maker, Keita Mori, a kind, lonely immigrant from Japan. Although Mori seems harmless, a chain of unexplainable ev</span>
  <span id="freeText4784994092180523865" style="display:none">1883. Thaniel Steepleton returns home to his tiny London apartment to find a gold pocket watch on his pillow. Six months later, the mysterious timepiece saves his life, drawing him away from a blast that destroys Scotland Yard. At last, he goes in search of its maker, Keita Mori, a kind, lonely immigrant from Japan. Although Mori seems harmless, a chain of unexplainable events soon suggests he must be hiding something. When Grace Carrow, an Oxford physicist, unwittingly interferes, Thaniel is torn between opposing loyalties. <br /><br />The Watchmaker of Filigree Street is a sweeping, atmospheric narrative that takes the reader on an unexpected journey through Victorian London, Japan as its civil war crumbles long-standing traditions, and beyond. Blending historical events with dazzling flights of fancy, it opens doors to a strange and magical past.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4784994092180523865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/663242-was-anyone-else-caught-off-guard-by-the"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Was anyone else caught off guard by the relationship between Thaniel and Mori? It came as a complete surprise to me; so much so that I had to reread the part where it came to fruition a couple times to make sure I wasn't misunderstanding. The lack of emotional description or build-up to it, or any reaction whatsoever by either character (relief, confusion, surprise), made this the most jarring part of the story for me <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_663242'><a id="like_count_community_question_663242" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/663242?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">12 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F22929563-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2418188-rochelle-mazar"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1396196561i/2418188._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2418188-rochelle-mazar">Rochelle Mazar</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Not even slightly caught off guard. Their relationship was beautifully built, I thought. They had several moments of romantic awkwardness that should <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Not even slightly caught off guard. Their relationship was beautifully built, I thought. They had several moments of romantic awkwardness that should have clued you in: Mori politely not turning around when Thaniel gets undressed when they first meet; Thaniel being bashful when Mori is in the tub and determinedly ensuring he could only see him from the shoulders up (suggesting that he's thinks about seeing him nude from the shoulders down, frankly); the way he takes Mori's hands after the boy injures him with the sword, and how Mori reacts to that gesture, as if things could have gone a different way starting from that point; the way Thaniel protects Mori so fiercely, which is sweet and kind of funny when you realize that Mori is clearly the most dangerous man in the world. But the first major clue is very early on, when Thaniel looks through Mori's book and translates it. In the book, Mori calls Thaniel "Thaniel". Mori told us from the start that he isn't comfortable using first names outside of very intimate relationships (only marriage). Once we learn that he writes things down from the vantage point of the future, it seemed like a pretty blatant hint that Mori would come to see Thaniel as his spouse in some variation on the future. And his changing accent? His accent was northern when his future was with Thaniel. Mori is also horrified when Grace takes care of her lab, and then the dining room, before considering where Thaniel's piano is going to go. I could only see that scene as Mori saying, "You won't love him the way I love him." It's all in there, it's just outside of the dialogue. I think it was beautifully handled.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

This question contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a href="/questions/585048-i-don-t-get-the-ending-so-mori"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i don't get the ending. So Mori deliberately sabotaged the train to delay &amp;/or kill Matsumoto? But he failed. What was the point of that? Matsumoto takes Grace away; wasn't that what Mori wanted? Very confusing.<br /><br />and the author lost me with the chase through the train tunnels. it seemed like she was trying to just END IT and threw everything together all at once, after the first 2/3 of the book was SO SLOOOOOW. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6183151-lindsay"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1359421104i/6183151._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6183151-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    No, Mori clearly sabotaged the train so that Matsumoto would see the news and return for Grace, thus giving her the happy ending that had always been <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    No, Mori clearly sabotaged the train so that Matsumoto would see the news and return for Grace, thus giving her the happy ending that had always been correct for her.<br /><br />And the business in the train tunnels was meant to be illogical and confusing - if it had been any other way Mori would have been able to predict Grace's actions and stop her. I have to disagree with you, the final third of the book moved much faster than the rest of the book. Breakneck speed in my opinion!<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1440669642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1440669642" />
    <a title="Robin Hobb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb"><img alt="Robin Hobb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450400p2/17730703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1440669642?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Hobb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Hobb" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb">Robin Hobb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1440669642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3517961890001428930">This is a tale that unfolds with the ticking precision of a fine timepiece. It doesn't hurry and it doesn't compromise. It definitely conveyed to me a feeling of a different time and a slightly different world.<br/><br/>The hardback itself is a lovely creation, with a keyhole cover, and a lovely font used throughout. The cover feels like suede. I mention this because it harmonizes so well with the atmosphere of the book. It feels as if I've picked up a book from another time and place.<br/><br/>In a sense, it could</span>
  <span id="freeText3517961890001428930" style="display:none">This is a tale that unfolds with the ticking precision of a fine timepiece. It doesn't hurry and it doesn't compromise. It definitely conveyed to me a feeling of a different time and a slightly different world.<br /><br />The hardback itself is a lovely creation, with a keyhole cover, and a lovely font used throughout. The cover feels like suede. I mention this because it harmonizes so well with the atmosphere of the book. It feels as if I've picked up a book from another time and place.<br /><br />In a sense, it could be categorized as steampunk, though I think Clockwork suits it admirably. It's a read to be savored rather than rushed through.<br /><br />I liked her characterizations especially. I felt she didn't require me to like all of her characters, but presented them as they were and let me pass my own judgements upon them. <br /><br />I will definitely watch for more books by Natasha Pulley. This is her debut novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3517961890001428930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1334571946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334571946" />
    <a title="Sean Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson"><img alt="Sean Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416866667p2/20955173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334571946?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Gibson" href="/user/show/20955173-sean-gibson">Sean Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334571946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4069110286280043249">Generally speaking, I’m fully on board with genre-defying/genre-bending works. Is this historical fiction? Steampunk? Mystery? Alternate history? Romance? Yes, sort of, a little, kind of, and yeah, sure. ("It's a taste treat! It's a laxative! Stop--you're BOTH right!")<br/><br/>Where I tend to start losing the thread and incur cramping of the cerebellum (which is only slightly less painful than a calf cramp in the middle of the night) is when time travel gets involved. Now, there’s not time travel going o</span>
  <span id="freeText4069110286280043249" style="display:none">Generally speaking, I’m fully on board with genre-defying/genre-bending works. Is this historical fiction? Steampunk? Mystery? Alternate history? Romance? Yes, sort of, a little, kind of, and yeah, sure. ("It's a taste treat! It's a laxative! Stop--you're BOTH right!")<br /><br />Where I tend to start losing the thread and incur cramping of the cerebellum (which is only slightly less painful than a calf cramp in the middle of the night) is when time travel gets involved. Now, there’s not time travel going on here, per se, but one of our primary characters, the inscrutable Keita Mori, is clairvoyant, which amounts to the same thing, particularly in the sense that as he intimates to various characters (particularly our protagonist, Thaniel Steepleton) his knowledge concerning the course of future events and subtly suggests how they might change them, that, in turn, changes his knowledge and perception of what is to come, resulting in the need to shove a banana into your ear so it can get to your brain (because potassium helps with cramps, right?). <br /><br />I loved the atmosphere of the story at the start—very Sherlockian, oozing with Victorianicity (which is now a word, as I have declared it to be so). As things progress, however, we move from mystery to history to (nearly) unrequited romance, a somewhat jarring shift in focus. The writing is lovely, and each component of the story, taken individually, has merit; it’s just that, when mashed together, it feels a little disjointed. It’s a little bit like putting whipped cream and parmesan cheese on a hamburger—individually, all good things, but none of them really feel quite right together, and you’re left with a funny expression on your face if you try to consume them all at once. (I know one of you weirdos is going to wax poetic on the merits of whipped cream on burgers, so let me just stop you right there and suggest a tongue transplant.)<br /><br />Ms. Pulley is a good writer and an imaginative storyteller—there’s enough promise here for me to keep an eye out for future works, even if this story didn’t totally work for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4069110286280043249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1249791308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249791308" />
    <a title="Blake Fraina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/860622-blake-fraina"><img alt="Blake Fraina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594167244p2/860622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249791308?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blake Fraina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blake Fraina" href="/user/show/860622-blake-fraina">Blake Fraina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408854280" href="/book/show/25121768-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249791308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6563410138304345227">All right, all you Sherlock Holmes fangirls, listen up.<br/><br/>What would you think of a version where “Sherlock” is a petite clairvoyant Japanese samurai/watchmaker with a Lincolnshire accent? And what if his “Watson” is a twenty-five year old Whitehall telegraph clerk who gave up his musical aspirations due to an acute case of synesthesia? And “Mary Watson” is an Oxford educated scientist with a butch haircut, a penchant for dressing in menswear and a Japanese dandy for a best friend? Think you might </span>
  <span id="freeText6563410138304345227" style="display:none">All right, all you Sherlock Holmes fangirls, listen up.<br /><br />What would you think of a version where “Sherlock” is a petite clairvoyant Japanese samurai/watchmaker with a Lincolnshire accent? And what if his “Watson” is a twenty-five year old Whitehall telegraph clerk who gave up his musical aspirations due to an acute case of synesthesia? And “Mary Watson” is an Oxford educated scientist with a butch haircut, a penchant for dressing in menswear and a Japanese dandy for a best friend? Think you might enjoy that?<br /><br />Let me answer that for you. Yes. Yes, you would.<br /> <br />Okay okay, this isn’t <i>really</i> a Sherlock Holmes story. But it’s as good as. And I mean that respectfully and in every respect. I know from a little online investigative work that author Natasha Pulley is a Sherlock fan, and this novel, which is surely an homage to Arthur Conan Doyle’s number one son, definitely ranks among the best of them. I haven’t enjoyed a book this much in a while. The atmosphere of Victorian era London is lovingly recreated. The characters are completely enchanting and believable - by the end I was in love with them all. And in typical Conan Doyle fashion, the plot is labyrinthine and kind of outrageous (as is the resolution), but that’s all part of the fun. Plus, there’s a neat fantasy element that is completely unique and charming.<br /><br />Like the entire oeuvre of recent Sherlock Holmes re-tellings, the focus is not really on the plot, which basically functions as nothing more than a convoluted Maguffin to deliver the real story – which is the relationship between these two very different men. I think readers will be delighted by the evident chemistry between the peculiar, misanthropic Keita Mori and hapless, pragmatist Nathaniel Steepleton.<br /><br />I hesitate to say more, for fear of spoiling a story that was full of truly wonderful surprises. I loved this book. I hated that it ended because I wanted to spend more time with these people. So even though it’s unbelievably corny and I vowed I would never say this sort of thing, I’m kind of wishing for a sequel.<br /><br />I’m confident this book will be a huge hit. It has all the right stuff.<br /><br />**GOOD NEWS, MY PRETTIES - According to this article/interview (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.theskinny.co.uk/books/features/stop-the-clocks-natasha-pulley-on-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">http://www.theskinny.co.uk/books/feat...</a>), Pulley has finished the sequel and is working on the final installment of the trilogy...Hooray!!**<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6563410138304345227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1278970426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278970426" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278970426?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408854280" href="/book/show/25121768-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278970426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5532099709102440214"><i>I received this advanced reading copy from the publisher with no requirement of review. All opinions and thoughts are my own.</i><br/><br/><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I think this book has so much potential. It follows Nathaniel ("Thaniel") Steepleton who works in the Home Office in London after he mysteriously receives a pocket watch that ends up saving his life. He meets the watchmaker, Mori, as well as precocious, intellectual woman named Grace, and all of their stories come together to *sort of* solve a mystery. <br/><br/>I say "sort</span>
  <span id="freeText5532099709102440214" style="display:none"><i>I received this advanced reading copy from the publisher with no requirement of review. All opinions and thoughts are my own.</i><br /><br /><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />I think this book has so much potential. It follows Nathaniel ("Thaniel") Steepleton who works in the Home Office in London after he mysteriously receives a pocket watch that ends up saving his life. He meets the watchmaker, Mori, as well as precocious, intellectual woman named Grace, and all of their stories come together to *sort of* solve a mystery. <br /><br />I say "sort of" because really there isn't much plot to this book. It develops sort of in the latter half of the book, and so I think with more editing and revising, and bringing some of that conflict and action to the beginning more, the book could be a lot better.<br /><br />My main issue with this book was that it just felt very confusing. Characters' motives, the choppy, obscure dialogue, and a lot of unresolved threads or open-ended scenes left me feeling a bit disoriented in the end. For most of the book I was unsure if I was confused because I was <i>supposed to be</i> confused and it would resolve later or if it was just written in a confusing way. It turns out to be the latter.<br /><br />I enjoyed the Victorian London, Sherlockian, semi-steampunkish fantasy elements of the story. But when it was 95% historical fiction with only about 5% fantasy elements, it seemed a bit unrealistic that <u>no one</u> in the story was ever really surprised by the fantastical bits. They all just accepted it as fact or went along with it with very little convincing.<br /><br />As for the characters, I never really grew attached to them because I didn't feel as though I ever really got to know them. Their dialogue, at times, was fairly unrealistic or convoluted, so I couldn't always follow their internal dialogue/thoughts in order to understand their motives. Basically, there were more than a couple times where things people said or did seemed illogical, and that kept me at a distance from the story.<br /><br />Overall, like I said before, I think with some rearranging of plot points, deeper development of characters, and sprucing up the dialogue, this book could be a big hit. It has some really intriguing and wonderful elements--albeit, some slightly racist undertones? (maybe it's the 1883 setting?)--that make for a potentially fun experience. But in the end, I was left feeling underwhelmed by my experience. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5532099709102440214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1381837613" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381837613" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1388593826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1388593826" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1388593826?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1388593826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4003500897283642234">I pity every booklover who unwittingly falls for the beautiful cover art and enticing story description as I did. The story is written in such a convoluted, amateur fashion, it requires significant work to stay invested while reading. Further, the story itself is incredibly dull and boring; in fact, the book seems void of any plot whatsoever. <br/><br/>I tried to plod through the book, eventually resorting to reading one chapter a day, then one chapter a week, but it was a grueling business. Often, I fini</span>
  <span id="freeText4003500897283642234" style="display:none">I pity every booklover who unwittingly falls for the beautiful cover art and enticing story description as I did. The story is written in such a convoluted, amateur fashion, it requires significant work to stay invested while reading. Further, the story itself is incredibly dull and boring; in fact, the book seems void of any plot whatsoever. <br /><br />I tried to plod through the book, eventually resorting to reading one chapter a day, then one chapter a week, but it was a grueling business. Often, I finished reading a chapter and thought: Why did the author even include this chapter? What was the purpose? What was I -- the reader -- supposed to take away from this? None of those questions ever had a clear answer; most of the book seems superfluous and irrelevant. <br /><br />The characters are forgettable, and the author's incompetent use of words like 'he' or 'him' and 'they' or 'them,' along with a fair number of typos, makes the actions of characters and their dialogue very difficult to follow. <br /><br />I cannot fathom how anyone signed off on this book being published. <br /><br />Many other reviews resort to naming the book's one redeeming quality: the presence of a clockwork octopus. If that's your bag, then I suggest you save your money, not buy this book, and instead pick up a copy of <i>Mortal Engines</i> by Philip Reeve. <br /><br />Finally, I confess here that I did not finish reading this book, making it the fourth (or perhaps fifth) book I've ever walked away from without finishing; I simply refuse to waste another minute of my life reading this abysmal novel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4003500897283642234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1289596807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289596807" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6217162-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430955688p2/6217162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289596807?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/6217162-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289596807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2501247051321368873">This book was written by a first time author which I was excited about. I usually enjoy reading books by newcomers because I feel as if I'm discovering them, myself, and can tell everyone about them. Their debut novels are often special enough for them to fight to get them published without a proven track record. And this book looked as if it would meet my expectations with its beautiful three dimensional cover and its intriguing premise. <br/><br/>The story takes place in Victorian England where Thaniel,</span>
  <span id="freeText2501247051321368873" style="display:none">This book was written by a first time author which I was excited about. I usually enjoy reading books by newcomers because I feel as if I'm discovering them, myself, and can tell everyone about them. Their debut novels are often special enough for them to fight to get them published without a proven track record. And this book looked as if it would meet my expectations with its beautiful three dimensional cover and its intriguing premise. <br /><br />The story takes place in Victorian England where Thaniel, a telegraphist for the Home Office, receives a mysterious gift from someone who broke into his place--a finely crafted pocket watch which wouldn't open until six months later, when it sounded a warning that saved his life during a political bombing. Soon Thaniel meets the mysterious watchmaker, Mr. Mori, a Japanese immigrant of noble blood, who creates beautiful clockwork figures. The Home Office feels Mr. Mori may be connected to the bombings, and even as Thaniel begins to form a tentative friendship with Mori, his employer asks that Thaniel gather possible evidence against him. Complicating matters when her path crosses Thaniel's is Grace Carrow, an independent minded, scholarly woman forced into giving up her research on natural ether unless a plan she hatches ensures her financial independence. <br /><br />So this sounded very interesting to me with its blend of steampunk, historical fiction, and political mystery, along with a good dose of the paranormal. But after reading only a few pages, I knew this book was in big trouble. Still, I kept reading it because it was a gift and because I kept hoping the wrinkles in the writing and the story would smooth out. But it would have taken a steam roller to accomplish that, or one very determined editor. <br /><br />I kept trying to figure out where the problem lay. I finally determined that the writing was so disjointed that nothing made sense without me rereading practically every other paragraph. Instead of the sentences flowing into one another to form a cohesive thought, action, or scene, it was as if the author had tossed sentences of her rough draft up into the air and wrote them down in the order in which they landed. Or it was as if only half of the ideas in her head made it to the page, leaving the reader to guess at what the other half were to understand the story. Here's an example of the disjointed writing you'll encounter when reading this book: <br /><br />'As the cab stopped gently on the gravel drive, he saw Mori on the balcony. Although he must have heard them, he did not look down. Threading his way through the foyer and the crowded stairway, where people had lined the rail to watch the dancing from above, Ito went up to him. Even the white men didn't have to duck to pass beneath the chrysanthemums.' <br /><br />So what does the word "them" in the second sentence refer to? The cab? A cab isn't a them. Perhaps it refers to the driver of the cab and its one occupant who aren't even talking to be heard? Perhaps it refers to the horses pulling the cab, of which there is no mention? And what the heck do chrysanthemums have to do with this paragraph? Talk about a non sequitur! And why should the reader care that they're tall, though I'm not getting a clear picture as to how they could be something for a person to walk beneath. Sheesh.<br /><br />This kind of writing is rampant in this book as well as the author focusing on minute details, such as how silk skirts hiss when someone wearing them walks, in favor of developing the character wearing the silk skirts. On it goes. The characters are mostly flat, bloodless, and unlikable, and they all sound alike, whether man or woman, young or old, British or Asian. Which brings me to this: there's a peppering of racial remarks throughout the book aimed at Asians and other non British persons. I'm not sure why the offensive remarks are in here, especially when everyone sounds the same and pretty much looks the same. One of the main characters, who's Asian, has bleached his hair blond and cut it very short. How very strange for a story taking place in the 1880's. <br /><br />Here's one more example of some of the writing that had me scratching my head: <br /><br />'The snow came down and silently down. There was snow in his thoughts, too. Matsumoto had been afraid. So had Grace. Through the snow, he couldn't see whether it was because they both understood things he hadn't, or because they had failed to understand something. And so he couldn't tell whether he had just watched Mori go to do what he had said, or just what Grace had said he would.' Righty-o. Got that drift on the third reading. <br /><br />Was there any saving grace to this book besides its beautiful cover? There were a few elements in the muddled story that kept me plodding through it. One of the main characters has two very special talents, one obvious and one hidden, both of them intriguing. And there's the clockwork itself, one of the figures an endearing octopus. And around the two thirds mark, the characters and story took a turn that twisted this book on its head. But none of this was enough for me to even come close to recommending this book to anyone even though a number of people have praised it. Still, I'll treasure my copy, a surprise gift--"just because"--from my younger daughter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2501247051321368873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1262540380" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1262540380" />
    <a title="Wart Hill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4621717-wart-hill"><img alt="Wart Hill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456668366p2/4621717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1262540380?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wart Hill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wart Hill" href="/user/show/4621717-wart-hill">Wart Hill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408854280" href="/book/show/25121768-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4621717-wart-hill?shelf=arc2015">arc2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4621717-wart-hill?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262540380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18434523751312112106"><a href='http://thingsifindwhileshelving.tumblr.com/post/117795665826/arc-review-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things I Find While Shelving</a><br/><br/><i>I received a free ARC via NetGalley</i><br/><br/>ARC Review: The Watchmaker of Filigree Street by Natasha Pulley<br/><br/>I did not enter this book expecting a gorgeous love story.<br/><br/>But I got one.<br/><br/>And damn is it good.<br/><br/>Thaniel works as a telegraphist in the Home Office and there've been a series of threats made by Irish nationalists - bomb threats. One night, Thaniel finds a strange watch has been left in his home. A watch that he cannot get to open. Then it opens by itself one day, and that day </span>
  <span id="freeText18434523751312112106" style="display:none"><a href="http://thingsifindwhileshelving.tumblr.com/post/117795665826/arc-review-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street" rel="nofollow noopener">Things I Find While Shelving</a><br /><br /><i>I received a free ARC via NetGalley</i><br /><br />ARC Review: The Watchmaker of Filigree Street by Natasha Pulley<br /><br />I did not enter this book expecting a gorgeous love story.<br /><br />But I got one.<br /><br />And damn is it good.<br /><br />Thaniel works as a telegraphist in the Home Office and there've been a series of threats made by Irish nationalists - bomb threats. One night, Thaniel finds a strange watch has been left in his home. A watch that he cannot get to open. Then it opens by itself one day, and that day it sets off an alarm when Thaniel is mere feet from where a bomb has been placed, ringing mere moments before the bomb goes off.<br /><br />This leads Thaniel to the watch's maker - one Keita Mori, a noble cum watchmaker from Japan. Thaniel is, of course, a bit suspicious of Mori because the watch knew when the bomb would go off. Add to that the fact that the bomb was timed with clockwork and, well...the police are behind Thaniel's suspicions and Thaniel opts to rent a room in Mori's shop to keep an eye on him.<br /><br />Except then Mori and Thaniel develop this beautiful friendship. And the better Thaniel knows Mori, the more convinced he is that Mori could not be behind the bombings, despite the conclusions the Yard's clockwork expert comes to: that the clockwork parts were made in Mori's style with Mori's parts.<br /><br />Thaniel has also gotten a new job in the Foreign Office, which leads him to a party where he meets a young scientist named Grace Carrow. After this meeting, Mori lets slip a few things he could not have known without having followed Thaniel. And Thaniel's suspicions are roused once again. Mori's explanation? He remembers the future. He tells Thaniel a series of things that will happen when he meets Grace the next day, and they do. And Thaniel tells Grace, who is intrigued and disbelieving. She develops a test.<br /><br />Mori passes this test, but he cannot predict completely random events. (For instance, he has a clockwork octopus with random gears so he never knows precisely where he's gonna wind up. I love the clockwork octopus. His name is Kazu).<br /><br />Grace and Thaniel wind up coming to an agreement to get married because Thaniel likes Grace and Grace needs to get married to inherit the house her aunt left and the laboratory space it provides. All seems to be going along splendidly until Grace expresses concern about Thaniel's relationship with Mori. She's afraid that Thaniel has been with Mori so long Mori has shaped him into one of his clockwork devices. So when he goes to see Mori on their wedding night, she devises a plan to get Thaniel away from him once and for all.<br /><br />And it's a shitty, shitty plan. Like. I get her reasoning and her logic, but omg it's amazing how foolish an intelligent person can act. And all I could think through the whole reveal was "why don't you marry Thaniel, let him have Mori, and you get the lab!"<br /><br />Happy times. Happy times.<br /><br />Instead she fucks up. Really bad. And it sucks, but people fuck up.<br /><br />And Mori and Thaniel remain adorable.<br /><br />I loved this book. A lot. Grace annoyed me sometimes, but like I said I can understand her logic for most things. Honestly, I may just love it for the beauty that is Mori and Thaniel's friendship. Either way. Gorgeous book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4670802130986928726">Absolutely loved this book. <br/><br/>An intricate maze of clockwork that spirals out with easy charm until you see the greater picture.<br/><br/>Characters are complex, charming yet flawed. And there's a clockwork octopus! (<i>that might have been what convinced me to buy!</i>)<br/><br/>Grace who would be the heroine of another book, so clever, held back by her gender, yet she has a Sherlockian disregard of people and lacks romance in her mathamatical soul.<br/>Matsumoto, sharp beneath his pretty veneer.<br/>Quiet Mori; gentle charm, coils,</span>
  <span id="freeText4670802130986928726" style="display:none">Absolutely loved this book. <br /><br />An intricate maze of clockwork that spirals out with easy charm until you see the greater picture.<br /><br />Characters are complex, charming yet flawed. And there's a clockwork octopus! (<i>that might have been what convinced me to buy!</i>)<br /><br />Grace who would be the heroine of another book, so clever, held back by her gender, yet she has a Sherlockian disregard of people and lacks romance in her mathamatical soul.<br />Matsumoto, sharp beneath his pretty veneer.<br />Quiet Mori; gentle charm, coils, whimsey and tea, yet he strikes fear in many.<br />Thaniel the main pov character, a simple self-sacrificing man, who sees colour and locks his dreams away.<br /><br />Genial policemen and the blunt force of the law. Everything is layered. The whole story has an air of magic and the joy is more in exploring the characters, their attitudes and how they fit together, than the mystery plot. Romance is subtle yet powerful, it feels strong though barely on the page.<br /><br />I finished and went immediately to the audio which is also a delight.<br />A firm favourite, I loved this story and will be reading it again.</span>

<div id="review_2449119227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449119227" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449119227?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=setting-porn">setting-porn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2019">z-read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449119227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9805949918761337423">This is a strange and very wonderful book about making clocks, the future, and also love in the 1850s. <br/><br/><i>The Watchmaker of Filigree Street</i> follows Thaniel, a local clerk who finds a watch on his person. When this watch alerts him of a bomb about to go off, his suspicions lead him to Mori, a Japanese clockmaker who is strangely kind to him. <br/><br/>Pretty cool setup, right? We don’t get a strong sense of Thaniel right off the bat; Mori, meanwhile, comes off as ambiguous but always strangely likeable. There</span>
  <span id="freeText9805949918761337423" style="display:none">This is a strange and very wonderful book about making clocks, the future, and also love in the 1850s. <br /><br /><i>The Watchmaker of Filigree Street</i> follows Thaniel, a local clerk who finds a watch on his person. When this watch alerts him of a bomb about to go off, his suspicions lead him to Mori, a Japanese clockmaker who is strangely kind to him. <br /><br />Pretty cool setup, right? We don’t get a strong sense of Thaniel right off the bat; Mori, meanwhile, comes off as ambiguous but always strangely likeable. There is also another character, Grace, who shows up and slowly becomes a part of the book’s narrative. It is weird, and atmospheric, and very interesting to see the cogs turn. <br /><br />The thing is that there is very little I can say about this book without at least vague spoilers, because the entire thing is a bit of a let’s-go-in-and-fuck-with-your-head-a-bit. So. <b>If you’re okay with a spoiler for fifty pages in, you can continue this review.</b><br /><br />We get the sense very early on that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mori can sense the future, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> simply by an amalgation of his clear knowledge of the watch and his actions in the past Japan-chapters. And I absolutely loved how the author played with this power as something fallible. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mori can predict friendships far into the future, but cannot detect based on the fall of a coin. There’s a tidbit about Mori’s accent that I really loved – he predicts that he won’t be seeing Thaniel very much anymore, and so his English accent loses its definition. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This definition becomes one of the main conflicts of the book and is played with an extremely deft hand. <br /><br />There is also a romance, and I want to talk about something here. At one point in the book, Thaniel participates in a marriage of convenience to Grace, and when he alerts Mori of this, he thinks to himself that he is stealing years of their strangely-close-roommates relationship from him. At this point in the book they’re not in any type of relationship; they’re simply living together, but he still feels as if he has lost something in giving up this living arrangement.<br /><br />I’ve brought this up before, but I think there’s something unbearably tender about <b>loving someone so deeply as a best friend that you don’t notice your feelings have turned romantic.</b> With being queer comes a lack of ability to notice the difference, sometimes, and a weird penchant for falling head over heels for friends you love too much to ever ask or expect anything from. It was incredible to see that explored so explicitly. <br /><br />While the narrative does at times explicitly challenge racism against Japanese characters, <b>some xenophobia within the narrative goes unchallenged</b>; an off-color remark about kimonos is perhaps realistic for a white character in 1800s Britain, but sort of in bad taste to go uncriticized. The treatment of lady suffragettes also struck me as odd; they are treated by Grace like idiots, and the narrative does not implicitly criticize this. Grace is not on any level written to be a voice of reason within the narrative, but I did wonder about the narrative purpose of these bits. <br /><br />On the whole, however, I thought this was a fun and very engaging ride, and would love to read more. I honestly am not sure how to sum up why I liked this so much – it’s a book about the conflict between fate and chance, and also an imaginative clockwork fantasy, and also somewhat of a mystery, and also very Tender love story, and the finale is... Wild, and I honestly just really enjoyed this. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4E3o" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9805949918761337423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1293499383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293499383" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1293499383?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Golden Compass fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ivonne by: </span>
      NetGalley
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293499383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16764178352786417888">In mid-1880s London, both Nathaniel “Thaniel” Steepleton, a 25-year-old lowly clerk and telegraphist first at the Home Office and then at the Foreign Office, and Grace Carrow, opinionated Oxford-trained physicist and daughter of old-fashioned Lord Carrow, both end up with a marvel of a timepiece. Both of these watches were lovingly crafted by a most unusual watchmaker, Keita Mori, related to a Samurai lord and a former assistant to the interior minister of Japan. These days Mori creates the fine</span>
  <span id="freeText16764178352786417888" style="display:none">In mid-1880s London, both Nathaniel “Thaniel” Steepleton, a 25-year-old lowly clerk and telegraphist first at the Home Office and then at the Foreign Office, and Grace Carrow, opinionated Oxford-trained physicist and daughter of old-fashioned Lord Carrow, both end up with a marvel of a timepiece. Both of these watches were lovingly crafted by a most unusual watchmaker, Keita Mori, related to a Samurai lord and a former assistant to the interior minister of Japan. These days Mori creates the finest watches in London. Scotland Yard suspect Mori’s mechanisms of being the heart of a series of bombs set by Irish nationalists, but Steepleton knows better. He recognizes that the tiny, gentle creator of the delightful Katsu, the clockwork, sock-stealing octopus, is no bomb maker. But there <i>is</i> much more to Mori than anyone would ever suspect. <br /><br />To tell any more would be to spoil this charming debut by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8446650.Natasha_Pulley" title="Natasha Pulley" rel="nofollow noopener">Natasha Pulley</a>, one that celebrates the most unlikely of romances. Despite the frequent comparisons to the Sherlock Holmes oeuvre, <i> The Watchmaker of Filigree Street</i> reminded me more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3618.Philip_Pullman" title="Philip Pullman" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip Pullman</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/119322.The_Golden_Compass__His_Dark_Materials___1_" title="The Golden Compass (His Dark Materials, #1) by Philip Pullman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Golden Compass</a> and its alternative clockwork world. Pulley’s wildly inventive tale kept me turning pages to the final startling revelations — although, in truth, the novel proves phenomenally original at nearly every turn. Highly recommended as one of the best books I’ve read in years.<br /><br />In the interest of full disclosure, I received this book from NetGalley and Bloomsbury USA in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16764178352786417888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1670637854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1670637854" />
    <a title="Helle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6909470-helle"><img alt="Helle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430669590p2/6909470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1670637854?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helle" href="/user/show/6909470-helle">Helle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6909470-helle?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1670637854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15571369636994950262">A whimsical, difficult-to-classify, atmospheric, speculative novel of the kind I haven’t read in years but which I was ultimately (surprisingly) pleased was suggested in one of my reading groups. I felt a slight whiff of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus' title='The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Night Circus</a>, a tiny hint of steampunk and the suggestion of inspiration from Philip Pullman. And yet the novel is entirely original.<br/><br/>The setting: Victorian London, and Japan.<br/><br/>The characters: a young telegrapher called Thaniel, a Japanese watchmaker called Mori, a young Oxfor</span>
  <span id="freeText15571369636994950262" style="display:none">A whimsical, difficult-to-classify, atmospheric, speculative novel of the kind I haven’t read in years but which I was ultimately (surprisingly) pleased was suggested in one of my reading groups. I felt a slight whiff of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Night Circus</a>, a tiny hint of steampunk and the suggestion of inspiration from Philip Pullman. And yet the novel is entirely original.<br /><br />The setting: Victorian London, and Japan.<br /><br />The characters: a young telegrapher called Thaniel, a Japanese watchmaker called Mori, a young Oxford-based scientist called Grace, a girl orphan called Six, some Whitehall civil servants, an anglified Japanese dandy, other minor English and Japanese characters.<br /><br />The plot: One evening, in his dingy Pimlico flat, Thaniel finds a fantastically delicate watch mysteriously left for him by an unknown and uninvited guest. Around the same time, Irish Clan na Gael (Fenian Brotherhood) have threatened to bomb Scotland Yard, a bombing which really took place in 1884 and for which the Fenians took credit. The watch warns Thaniel at the last minute, and he manages to save his life, but this ignites his curiosity – and that of the Yard – and he is off to Filigree Street where the maker of said watch lives. <br /><br />Mori’s little watchmaker shop is full of dainty clockwork: watches, small birds, fireflies and a small octopus called Katsu. The meeting between Thaniel and Mori sets off a series of events which the rest of the book explores, going down various routes into a Japanese past and possible English futures. Along the way, we discover how Thaniel sees colours in sounds, how Grace believes in the existence of ether in the air, and how Mori’s memories are not what we, or Thaniel, at first thought. <br /><br />Style: What raises this novel from yet another potential steampunk-ish pastiche with elements from magical realism (not fantasy) were the quirky sentences, the interest in turning out a good phrase to either explore character or create an ambience, and the occasional philosophical musings. It is not a plot-based page-turner. In fact, it took me some 60-70 pages to really latch on to the story, and there were some confusing moments along the way, not least in some of the dialogues. But the last third or so was magical, and it appeared that some of the confusion had been deliberate. <br /><br />Below a few extracts, though there were many more:<br /><br /><i>War was punching the clock instead of looking at the broken mechanisms.<br /><br />She moved like a faulty bicycle, by turns too fast, and then too slowly.</i> (And later, about the same character:) <i> Her joints were moving badly, all unoiled hydraulics. <br /><br />There were a dozen languages fluttering under the chandeliers. <br /><br />Matsumoto gave him the amused look of an experienced dandy meeting his younger self.<br /><br />He tried to feel around the idea of prison. The edges of it were too sharp to touch.</i><br /><br />And of course, the cover is suitably whimsical and lovely with a little peep hole through which you can see the numbers on the watch. Not something I would normally ‘fall for’, but upon closing I seemed to have changed my mind. I was charmed by this book.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15571369636994950262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3201526990" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3201526990" />
    <a title="Anna Luce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce"><img alt="Anna Luce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604227738p2/9429655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3201526990?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Luce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Luce" href="/user/show/9429655-anna-luce">Anna Luce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=5-good-reads">5-good-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=2020-reviews">2020-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9429655-anna-luce?shelf=audiobooks-i-own">audiobooks-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3201526990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11421092227208463185">★★★★✰ 3.5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>“Under the gas lamps, mist pawed at the windows of the closed shops, which became steadily shabbier nearer home. It was such a smooth ruination that he could have been walking forward through time, watching the same buildings age five years with every step, all still as a museum”.</blockquote><br/><br/><i>The Watchmaker of Filigree Street</i> mostly takes place during the 1880s in London. One of the main characters is twenty-five year old Thaniel Steepleton who works as a telegraph clerk at the Home Office. Hi</span>
  <span id="freeText11421092227208463185" style="display:none">★★★★✰ 3.5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote>“Under the gas lamps, mist pawed at the windows of the closed shops, which became steadily shabbier nearer home. It was such a smooth ruination that he could have been walking forward through time, watching the same buildings age five years with every step, all still as a museum”.</blockquote><br /><br /><i>The Watchmaker of Filigree Street</i> mostly takes place during the 1880s in London. One of the main characters is twenty-five year old Thaniel Steepleton who works as a telegraph clerk at the Home Office. His mundane and solitary existence is thrown into upheaval after<b> a mysterious pocket watch saves him from a terrorist time bomb</b>. Believing that the maker of his watch is somehow connected to this attack, under false pretences Thaniel moves into the watchmaker’s residence on Filigree Street. The watchmaker, who goes by his surname, Mori, hails from Japan. Mori, who seems to have a polite and quiet disposition, is more than happy to have Thaniel around. Thaniel too finds himself warming up to Mori and his customs. While Thaniel soon realises that his new landlord is indeed hiding things from him, he questions whether his involvement in the terrorist attack.<br />Alongside Thaniel’s story we also read of Grace Carrow who studies physics at Oxford. Grace wants to pursue her studies and experiments but thanks to her parents she will only be able to do so as a married woman. Given that no one seems interested in marrying such an ‘uncompromising’ and ‘eccentric’ woman, Grace has few options left...<br />While Thaniel and Grace’s paths do eventually converge, readers might be surprised by the consequences of their acquaintanceship.<br /><br /><b>Thaiel and Mori were easily my favourite characters.</b> There is a faltering quality to their friendship. In spite of their age, class, and cultural differences they soon became used to one another. <br />For the most part Grace struck me as the usual protagonist of certain contemporary historical novels, which often star heroines who are unfeminine and uninterested in marrying or adhering to the social norms of their time. Her main characteristic is her ambition, which does make her somewhat admirable. Later on <i>however</i> she makes some increasingly maddening choices that were not clearly explained.<br /><br />Natasha Pulley does an excellent job in giving her story a <b>Victorian atmosphere</b>. Whether she was writing about London or Japan I found her historicism to be<b> accurate and evocative</b>. Her novel’s storyline could be best described as being <b>part period mystery, part gentle adventure</b>. One of the main ideas the story plays around with is as clever as it is fascinating...so much so that part of me wants to reread this book in order to pick up on what I’d initially glossed over.<br /><br />The narrative also has a lot of<b> steampunk elements</b>—which range from gaslights to clockwork automatons—as well aspects that struck me as belonging to the magical realism genre. <br />I particularly appreciated the realistic depiction of being a Japanese expatriate in Victorian London. Mori, alongside other Japanese characters, is routinely exposed to racist behaviour and attitudes. Grace’s story instead emphasises the way in which gender discrimination oppressed, repressed, or constrained women lives.<br />A portion of the narrative is also dedicated to Japan. Here we read of the divide and conflict between <b>conservatism and Westernisation</b>, which made for some engaging reading material.<br /><br />The budding friendship between Thaniel and Mori was extremely sweet and filled with <b>a quiet sort of yearning</b>, for above all companionship. Part of me wishes that instead of having sections dedicated to Grace we could have had some more insight into Mori’s character as he was a lot more interesting. Grace’s later behaviour made her particularly unlikable...yet the narrative seems to imply that we should condone her actions. <br /><br />Grace aside, I really loved this novel. It is<b> a slow-burn mystery</b> and not for those who are looking for anything too ostentatiously fantastic. Pulley’s writing is <b>a pure pleasure to read</b>: from her vivid descriptions to her humour. What began as a seemingly unassuming story soon conveyed brilliant depths.<br />I thoroughly recommend this one, especially to fans of Victorian settings or steampunk.<br /><br /><a href="https://wishfullyreading.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Read more reviews on my blog</a> / / / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/9429655-anna-luce" rel="nofollow noopener">View all my reviews on Goodreads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11421092227208463185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1435836437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435836437" />
    <a title="Mary Robinette Kowal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2808402-mary-robinette-kowal"><img alt="Mary Robinette Kowal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602692414p2/2808402.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Robinette Kowal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Robinette Kowal" href="/user/show/2808402-mary-robinette-kowal">Mary Robinette Kowal</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14846296439115431859">It is 4:45am and I have just finished this astonishingly good novel. I knew nothing about it other than that it had a lovely cover, and that the first page was beautifully written. It's historical fantasy, set in London and Japan. The language is vivid and compelling. The characters are achingly real. I could tell you about the plot, but I think you will like it best if you discover it yourself.<br/><br/>Just make sure you have plenty of spare time, because it is very hard to put down.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1865294241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865294241" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865294241?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/36435488-the-watchmaker-of-filigree-street">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=magical-realism-mastery">magical-realism-mastery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=historical-highness">historical-highness</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865294241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15990339374388859268">This book was a total cover boy, a few years ago, and then I added it to my shelves and never felt the urge to pick it up again. A recent purge of my shelves had me re-evaluating many of the titles there, however, and finally hastened me to give this a read. I am SO glad I did!<br/><br/>I had assumed this to be a straight-forward historical mystery but was pleasantly surprised to also find this a whimsical cross-cultural tale with a hefty dose of magical realism and murky steampunk tones, throughout.<br/><br/>This </span>
  <span id="freeText15990339374388859268" style="display:none">This book was a total cover boy, a few years ago, and then I added it to my shelves and never felt the urge to pick it up again. A recent purge of my shelves had me re-evaluating many of the titles there, however, and finally hastened me to give this a read. I am SO glad I did!<br /><br />I had assumed this to be a straight-forward historical mystery but was pleasantly surprised to also find this a whimsical cross-cultural tale with a hefty dose of magical realism and murky steampunk tones, throughout.<br /><br />This book is heavy on its description and the flowery language perfectly encapsulated the whimsy of the tale it depicted. Central characters, Thaniel and Mori, also make this a delightful read and if their adorable relationship isn't explicitly stated as being something more than friendship in the rumoured sequel I will SUE!<br /><br />The only slight mar on the excellence of this piece is the open-ended nature of the conclusion. I found I still had many questions, when turning the final page, and much of the mystery was too neatly packaged whilst other portions were neglected entirely.<br /><br />However, my final dissatisfaction was minor in comparison with my overall enjoyment. This remained bizarre and bewildering throughout, but what else could I expect from a book that featured a clockwork octopus named Katsu, with a penchant for petty theft and closet drawers!?</span>

    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10694687-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461864114p2/10694687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1331436743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9668353539687942919">This was described to me as a wittier and twistier Sherlock Holmes (with a samurai! With that awesome cover! When will I ever learn that the old adage about not judging a book actually means something?), and I'm disappointed to say that it didn't live up to its potential at all. It was confusing, disjointed, the dialogue felt clunky and awkward, and I felt that the characters deserved a better story. <br/><br/>But at least the clockwork octopus was amazing. Fuller review to come eventually.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5299510062234628277">From my first read Autumn 2016:<br/><br/>There were problems with the plot in places, I think it suffered from “too many cooks/authors” syndrome, in that the author may have taken too much advice from too many people and that it shows? I don’t know why I think this, it’s just an impression I have.<br/><br/>However, most importantly this is a rollicking good story!   <span id="freeText5299510062234628277" style="display:none">From my first read Autumn 2016:<br /><br />There were problems with the plot in places, I think it suffered from “too many cooks/authors” syndrome, in that the author may have taken too much advice from too many people and that it shows? I don’t know why I think this, it’s just an impression I have.<br /><br />However, most importantly this is a rollicking good story! I enjoyed it immensely, an almost magical clockwork pet octopus, foreseeing the probable future, clockwork bombs, is he a villain or a hero and if so can we be friends or more than friends? watches that find their owners again when they get lost – together all these elements make a really good enjoyable story. <br /><br />That after all, in my opinion, is the primary purpose of fiction.<br /><br />Thoughts on my second read early Summer 2020:<br /><br />Once more on reading this I loved the elements of the story, I am once more charmed by Mori's remembering and forgetting of past events, clockwork pets, and the strange mix of magical realism and steampunk throughout the novel. However, there is definitely something wrong with the narrative flow. If this was one of Mori's watched it would have all of the pretty jewels but the clockwork would be misaligned. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
